--- layout: default title: "ManyBinTxt - Many TXT Records with Binary Data" parent: "Fuzzing" --- ManyBinTxt - Many TXT Records with Binary Data

ManyBinTxt - Many TXT Records with Binary Data

This module is designed to respond with arbitrary number of TXT records, each containing data of arbitrary size.

Typically, a TXT record consists of one or more labels, and each label can be up to 255 bytes in size. If the required data size exceeds this limit, multiple labels are used within the same TXT record to accommodate the data.

This flexibility allows for generating very large DNS responses, up to the maximum allowable DNS packet size of 65535 bytes.

In this variant, the labels are composed of random binary data.

Category: Fuzzing

RFCs: RFC1035, RFC1464

Format

manybintxt.<RECORDS>.<SIZE>.yourdomain.com

Where:

  • The <RECORDS> parameter specifies the number of TXT records to be included in the answer.

  • The <SIZE> parameter specifies the size of each TXT record. As mentioned in the description, a TXT record consists of one or more labels, and the maximum size of a single TXT label is 255 bytes. If the specified size exceeds this limit, multiple labels will be dynamically generated to accommodate the specified size.

Examples

In this example, we request to produce 10 TXT records, each containing 30 random bytes. As we can see, these 30 bytes fit easily within a single label:

# dig manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1

; <<>> DiG 9.18.10-2-Debian <<>> manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1
;; global options: +cmd
;; Got answer:
;; ->>HEADER<<- opcode: QUERY, status: NOERROR, id: 65528
;; flags: qr aa; QUERY: 1, ANSWER: 10, AUTHORITY: 0, ADDITIONAL: 0

;; QUESTION SECTION:
;manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. IN	A

;; ANSWER SECTION:
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\137vI\023\026\208\176\166\140p\241\218\148\203?\162\129\150\013\152N\029j\243\130Ob\203\216\158"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\163\205\009\200t\222\148\153\"\214\213s\187\181\153NR\020C\227\188\010\128\255\159\242y\194\174\224"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\165\017\014\209O\190i\247\001\2423*\000-\133pCu\1956:\237\"\164\023\\\200(7\166"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\128i+\148i|\168!\136\136\244\141\230sn)\197i[K\250R\151X\200\159\173_jj"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\"u\163\173\159\1552\219T\176PD\233+\182N\019\239>\007\012}\130\148\251\006\162S!\239"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"Y\018\1620\007\015P\164{%\245\003\\\228\000\224\255I;vq\000{\014\220V2*~\024"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\212\133\137\012\193M\152TVnT2H\226\226\242\023[\020xv\153\209\227\209Q\172Y\226X"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	".y\164h?\224?\158\\\140io/\209\223\190\213\226\153}\029\250\207+MN\153T\216\174"
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"\245S\008\129w\2439L\246\021uw\216!.\236\187\227jSh\135?\021z%\214\210\133["
manybintxt.10.30.yourdomain.com. 60 IN	TXT	"#\169\003\163\025,~\013\019\201\148\009v\139r\157\226[\024\176\206\018\137\236T\222\139\162e\241"

;; Query time: 3 msec
;; SERVER: 127.0.0.1#53(127.0.0.1) (UDP)
;; WHEN: Fri Jan 03 14:42:46 +04 2025
;; MSG SIZE  rcvd: 479

Download PCAP File


In this example, we request to produce 10 TXT records, each containing 300 random bytes. As we can see, these 300 bytes must be split into 2 labels, as the maximum size for a single label is 255 bytes:

# dig manybintxt.10.300.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1

; <<>> DiG 9.18.10-2-Debian <<>> manybintxt.10.300.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1

;; Got answer:
;; ->>HEADER<<- opcode: QUERY, status: NOERROR, id: 12871

;manybintxt.10.300.yourdomain.com. IN	A

Download PCAP File


In this example, we request to produce a single TXT record containing 50,000 random bytes. As we can see, this will be split into many labels:

# dig manybintxt.1.50000.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1

; <<>> DiG 9.18.10-2-Debian <<>> manybintxt.1.50000.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1
;; global options: +cmd
;; Got answer:
;; ->>HEADER<<- opcode: QUERY, status: NOERROR, id: 53141
;; flags: qr aa; QUERY: 1, ANSWER: 1, AUTHORITY: 0, ADDITIONAL: 0

;; QUESTION SECTION:
;manybintxt.1.50000.yourdomain.com. IN	A

;; ANSWER SECTION:
manybintxt.1.50000.yourdomain.com. 60 IN Like other features, you can append anything to the feature name to avoid receiving cached responses from the target DNS resolver. This forces the target resolver to actively communicate with our PolarDNS server instead of responding with cached answers. Using a random number is the most effective strategy:

# dig manybintxt${RANDOM}.10.30.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1

; <<>> DiG 9.18.10-2-Debian <<>> manybintxt23801.10.30.yourdomain.com @127.0.0.1
;; global options: +cmd
;; Got answer:
;; ->>HEADER<<- opcode: QUERY, status: NOERROR, id: 61135
;; flags: qr aa; QUERY: 1, ANSWER: 10, AUTHORITY: 0, ADDITIONAL: 0

;; QUESTION SECTION:
;manybintxt23801.10.30.yourdomain.com. IN A

;; ANSWER SECTION:
